<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>The recent standardization of radio frequency identification (RFID) operating at ultrahigh frequencies (UHFs) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a> has supported the diffusion of applications based on the transmission and reception of electromagnetic (EM) waves propagating between the Reader and the Tag, thus, potentially increasing the read-range with respect to the rather common RFID systems based on inductive, near-field coupling in the HF band (mainly at 13.56 MHz). Moreover, higher the frequency, higher the communication data-rate.</p><p>In many UHF RFID applications, the Transponder behaves as backscatter modulator: the reception of the unmodulated carrier transmitted by the Reader activates the integrated circuit (connected to the Tag antenna), which responds by varying its input impedance (i.e., the antenna load) thus modulating the backscattered field to the Reader <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>.</p><p>Therefore, the investigation of the backscattered contribution from the RFID Transponder represents an important and crucial issue in order to properly evaluate the behavior and the performance of UHF RFID systems. In the following, a complete analytical approach to the estimation of the backscattered radiated field by a UHF RFID Tag is presented and described.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Background on Antenna Scattering Theory</h2></div><p>It is well known that an object illuminated by an incoming wave scatters EM energy as the result of currents induced by the incident field <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_2">[4]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_2">[5]</a>. The total amount and the radiation pattern of the backscattered power depend on the geometrical and EM properties of the object (size, shape, constitutive materials, etc.).</p><p>In particular, objects designed as antennas or constituted of an antenna as main part can be associated with two different modes of scattering the incident energy, one independent of the antenna load impedance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z _{L}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-3"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-4" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-5"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-6"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-7" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">Z _{L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (structural mode scattering), the other strongly load-dependent (antenna mode scattering) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_2">[4]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_2">[5]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_2">[6]</a>.</p><p>According to the antenna scatterer theorem <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_2">[7]</a>, an antenna loaded by the impedance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z _{L}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-8" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-9"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-10"><span style="display: inline-block; <div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/4446029/4400938/4400938-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/4446029/4400938/4400938-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 2. </b><fig><p>Transmitting antenna and radiated field.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4400938/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>The first and the second term in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn1" href="#deqn1" class="fulltext-link">(1)</a> are usually referred as the structural and the antenna scattering mode, respectively; therefore, it is evident that the definitions of the scattering modes are rather arbitrary, since they depends on the considered reference case <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_2">[4]</a>.</p></div>

id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z _{L}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-46-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z _{L2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-48-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-48">Z _{L2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (load modulation) produces two different values of the power reflection coefficients (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{}\rho _{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-49-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-49">{}\rho _{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{}\rho _{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-50-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-50">{}\rho _{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) and therefore the modulation of the field scattered by the Tag which switches over the corresponding values <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{}\vec E_{\rm scat}^{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-51-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-51">{}\vec E_{\rm scat}^{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{}\vec E_{\rm scat}^{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-52-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-52">{}\vec E_{\rm scat}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><p>Since the whole scattered field doesn't generally depend only on the current induced at the antenna terminal, then <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{}\vec E_{\rm scat}^{\rm REF}/I_{\rm REF}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-53-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-53">{}\vec E_{\rm scat}^{\rm REF}/I_{\rm REF}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> cannot be evaluated through <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn3" href="#deqn3" class="fulltext-link">(3)</a> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">A \not= 1</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-54-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-54">A \not= 1</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. In general, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">A</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-55-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-55">A</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is a complex, load-independent coefficient related to the current induced on the antenna conducting surface by the incident wave <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_3">[10]</a>; its exact value is then dependent on the geometrical layout of the Tag antenna and the EM properties of the materials it is constituted of <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_3">[10]</a>.</p><p>Nevertheless, it is known that <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">A \approx 1</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-56-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-56">A \approx 1</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for thin dipole <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_3">[9]</a>, and therefore <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">A = 1</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-57-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-57">A = 1</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is often assumed as useful, rather reasonable approximation for the performance evaluation of general RFID system, since UHF RFID Transponder are usually equipped with thin, small, dipole-like antennas.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Further Considerations</h2></div><p><i>Transponder RCS</i>âby means of <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn9" href="#deqn9" class="fulltext-link">(9)</a>, both differentialâ<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{}\sigma (\theta, \phi)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-58-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-58">{}\sigma (\theta, \phi)</script></tex-math></inline-formula>âand totalâ<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{}\sigma _{T}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-59-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-59">{}\sigma _{T}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>âRCS <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_4">[4]</a> of the Tag can be estimated <disp-formula id="deqn10-11" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eqalignno{\sigma \left({\theta, \phi } \right) =&amp;\, 4\pi r^{2} \cdot {{\left\vert {\vec E_{\rm scat} } \right\vert^{2} } \over {\left\vert {\vec E_{\rm inc} } \right\vert^{2} }}\cr =&amp;\, {{\lambda ^{2} } \over {4\pi }} \cdot K \cdot \tau \cdot g\left({\theta _{\rm inc}, \phi _{\rm inc} } \right) \cdot g\left({\theta, \phi } \right)&amp; {\hbox{(10)}} \cr \sigma _{T} =&amp;\, 2\eta {{P_{bs} } \over {\left\vert {\vec E_{\rm inc} } \right\vert^{2} }} = {{\sigma \left({\theta, \phi } \right) \cdot \delta } \over {g\left({\theta, \phi } \right)}}\cr =&amp;\, {{\lambda ^{2} } \over {4\pi }} \cdot K \cdot \tau \cdot \delta \cdot g\left({\theta _{\rm inc}, \phi _{\rm inc} } \right) &amp; {\hbox{(11)}}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-60-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-60">\eqalignno{\sigma \left({\theta, \phi } \right) =&amp;\, 4\pi r^{2} \cdot {{\left\vert {\vec E_{\rm scat} } \right\vert^{2} } \over {\left\vert {\vec E_{\rm inc} } \right\vert^{2} }}\cr =&amp;\, {{\lambda ^{2} } \over {4\pi }} \cdot K \cdot \tau \cdot g\left({\theta _{\rm inc}, \phi _{\rm inc} } \right) \cdot g\left({\theta, \phi } \right)&amp; (apart from <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{}\tau </span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-67-Frame" In particular, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V _{\bmod}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-70-Frame" class="MathJax_Preview">(A-\rho _{1,2})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-82-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-82">(A-\rho _{1,2})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and, therefore <disp-formula id="deqn13" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V_{\bmod 1,2} = V_{0} \cdot \left({A - \rho _{1,2} } \right)\eqno {\hbox{(13)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-83-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-83">V_{\bmod 1,2} = V_{0} \cdot \left({A - \rho _{1,2} } \right)\eqno {\hbox{(13)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">V_{\bmod 1,2} = V_{0} \cdot \left({A - \rho _{1,2} } \right)\eqno {\hbox{(13)}}</span></span></disp-formula>where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V _{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-84-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-84">V _{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> represents the receiver input voltage normalized with respect to A and in case <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">Z _{L} = Z _{A} ^{\ast } (\rho = 0)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-85-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-85">Z _{L} = Z _{A} ^{\ast } (\rho = 0)</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p><p>Assuming modulation data encoded by the Tag according to FM0 or Miller coding schemes (as required in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_4">[1]</a>) and perfect matched-filter demodulation with ideal carrier recovery and equalization at the receiver (as considered in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_4">[3]</a>) the minimum <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(s _{\min})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-86-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-86">(s _{\min})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and maximum <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(s _{\max})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-87-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-87">(s _{\max})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> values at the input of the detector can be found to be, respectively, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">s _{\min} = 0</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-88-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-88">s _{\min} = 0</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <disp-formula id="deqn14" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">s_{\max } = {{\left\vert {V_{\bmod 1} - V_{\bmod 2} } \right\vert} \over 2} = {{\left\vert {V_{0} } \right\vert \cdot \left\vert {\rho _{1} - \rho _{2} } \right\vert} \over 2}\eqno {\hbox{(14)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-89-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-89">s_{\max } = {{\left\vert {V_{\bmod 1} - V_{\bmod 2} } \right\vert} \over 2} = {{\left\vert {V_{0} } \right\vert \cdot \left\vert {\rho _{1} - \rho _{2} } \right\vert} \over 2}\eqno {\hbox{(14)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">s_{\max } = {{\left\vert {V_{\bmod 1} - V_{\bmod 2} } \right\vert} \over 2} = {{\left\vert {V_{0} } \right\vert \cdot \left\vert {\rho _{1} - \rho _{2} } \right\vert} \over 2}\eqno {\hbox{(14)}}</span></span></disp-formula>for both ASK and PSK modulation.</p><p>Assuming the received signal corrupted by AWGN with standard deviation <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{}\sigma </span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-90-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-90">{}\sigma </script></tex-math></inline-formula> at the input of the detector (i.e., at the output of the matched filter), the BER at the Reader may be expressed as follows: <disp-formula id="deqn15" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eqalignno{{\rm BER} =&amp;\, {1 \over 2}{\rm erfc}\left({{{\left\vert {V_{\bmod 1} - V_{\bmod 2} } \right\vert} \over {4 \cdot \sqrt 2 \cdot \sigma }}} \right)\cr =&amp;\, {1 \over 2}{\rm erfc}\left({{{\left\vert {V_{0} } \right\vert \cdot m} \over {2 \cdot \sqrt 2 \cdot \sigma }}} \right) &amp; {\hbox{(15)}}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-91-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-91">\eqalignno{{\rm BER} =&amp;\, {1 \over 2}{\rm erfc}\left({{{\left\vert {V_{\bmod 1} - V_{\bmod 2} } \right\vert} \over {4 \cdot \sqrt 2 \cdot \sigma }}} \right)\cr =&amp;\, {1 \over 2}{\rm erfc}\left({{{\left\vert {V_{0} } \right\vert \cdot m} \over {2 \cdot \sqrt 2 \cdot \sigma }}} \right) &amp; {\hbox{(15)}}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\eqalignno{{\rm BER} =&amp;\, {1 \over 2}{\rm erfc}\left({{{\left\vert {V_{\bmod 1} - V_{\bmod 2} } \right\vert} \over {4 \cdot \sqrt 2 \cdot \sigma }}} \right)\cr =&amp;\, {1 \over 2}{\rm erfc}\left({{{\left\vert {V_{0} } \right\vert \cdot m} \over {2 \cdot \sqrt 2 \cdot \sigma }}} \right) &amp; {\hbox{(15)}}}</span></span></disp-formula>being <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">m = \vert \rho _{1} -\rho _{2} \vert /2</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-92-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-92">m = \vert \rho _{1} -\rho _{2} \vert /2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> the modulation index <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_4">[12]</a>. According to <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn15" href="#deqn15" class="fulltext-link">(15)</a>, it is worth noticing that the performance at the Reader is independent of the load-independent backscattering contributions (i.e., of the value of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">A</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-93-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-93">A</script></tex-math></inline-formula>); this result agrees with the one achieved in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_4">[13]</a>, where the differential RCS is found to be proportional to the modulation index m. Moreover, <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn15" href="#deqn15" class="fulltext-link">(15)</a> is still valid in case of multipath propagation <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_4">[14]</a>, provided that <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V _{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-94-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-94">V _{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> accounts of the interference between the multiple received contributions.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>The backscattered, modulated wave from UHF RFID Transponders is an important parameter which must be taken into account for both evaluation and design of RFID systems. Here, a theoretical and analytical formula for the backscattered field is presented and described. RCS and BER evaluations performed by means of the proposed analytical expression totally agree with the results achieved in several other available papers, thus demonstrating the validity of the present letter.</p></div>
</div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

		if(IBP_WS_ENABLED_FLAG){
		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>
